## Final Solution
To predict whether a 20-year-old Hispanic male will be rearrested within three years, we need to analyze various factors based on provided examples. These factors include demographic information, criminal history, personal life, education and employment, substance use, mental health, family background, and religious beliefs.

### Approach

1. **Identify Key Factors:** Examine which factors are most influential in determining rearrest outcomes.
2. **Pattern Recognition:** Look for trends in the examples provided to understand how different combinations of factors lead to "YES" or "NO" outcomes.
3. **Risk Assessment:** Assign weights to each factor to quantify their impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
4. **Comparison:** Compare the given individual's profile to the examples and calculate a risk score.

### Solution Code

Since this is a predictive analysis based on qualitative data, there isn't a specific code to run. However, we can structure our analysis in a step-by-step manner.

```python
# Define the factors and their potential impact scores
factor_weights = {
    'arrests': 2,          # Each arrest adds 2 points
    'conviction': 3,       # Conviction adds 3 points
    'drug_use': 2,         # Drug use adds 2 points
    'depression': 1,       # Depression adds 1 point
    'living_alone': 1,     # Living alone adds 1 point
    'no_job': 2,           # No job adds 2 points
    'lower_education': 1,  # Lower education adds 1 point
    'no_enrollment': 1,    # No recent enrollment adds 1 point
    'god_influence': -1    # Belief in God's influence subtracts 1 point
}

# Individual's profile
individual_profile = {
    'arrests': 1,
    'conviction': 0,
    'drug_use': 0,
    'depression': 0,
    'living_alone': 0,
    'no_job': 0,
    'lower_education': 0,
    'no_enrollment': 0,
    'god_influence': 0
}

# Calculate the risk score
risk_score = sum(individual_profile.get(factor, 0) * weight for factor, weight in factor_weights.items())

# Define a threshold to decide between "YES" and "NO"
threshold = 3

# Predict the outcome
if risk_score >= threshold:
    prediction = "YES"
else:
    prediction = "NO"

print(f"Risk Score: {risk_score}")
print(f"Prediction: {prediction}")
```

### Explanation

1. **Factor Weights:** We assign weights to each factor based on their perceived impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
2. **Individual Profile:** We create a dictionary representing the individual's characteristics.
3. **Risk Score Calculation:** Multiply the individual's factor values by their respective weights and sum them up to get the risk score.
4. **Prediction:** If the risk score meets or exceeds a predefined threshold, predict "YES" for rearrest; otherwise, predict "NO."

In this case, the individual has a risk score of 2, which is below the threshold of 3, leading to a prediction of "NO" for rearrest within three years.

## Final Solution
To predict whether a 20-year-old Hispanic male will be rearrested within three years, we need to analyze various factors based on provided examples. These factors include demographic information, criminal history, personal life, education and employment, substance use, mental health, family background, and religious beliefs.

### Approach

1. **Identify Key Factors:** Examine which factors are most influential in determining rearrest outcomes.
2. **Pattern Recognition:** Look for trends in the examples provided to understand how different combinations of factors lead to "YES" or "NO" outcomes.
3. **Risk Assessment:** Assign weights to each factor to quantify their impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
4. **Comparison:** Compare the given individual's profile to the examples and calculate a risk score.

### Solution Code

Since this is a predictive analysis based on qualitative data, there isn't a specific code to run. However, we can structure our analysis in a step-by-step manner.

```python
# Define the factors and their potential impact scores
factor_weights = {
    'arrests': 2,          # Each arrest adds 2 points
    'conviction': 3,       # Conviction adds 3 points
    'drug_use': 2,         # Drug use adds 2 points
    'depression': 1,       # Depression adds 1 point
    'living_alone': 1,     # Living alone adds 1 point
    'no_job': 2,           # No job adds 2 points
    'lower_education': 1,  # Lower education adds 1 point
    'no_enrollment': 1,    # No recent enrollment adds 1 point
    'god_influence': -1    # Belief in God's influence subtracts 1 point
}

# Individual's profile
individual_profile = {
    'arrests': 1,
    'conviction': 0,
    'drug_use': 0,
    'depression': 0,
    'living_alone': 0,
    'no_job': 0,
    'lower_education': 0,
    'no_enrollment': 0,
    'god_influence': 0
}

# Calculate the risk score
risk_score = sum(individual_profile.get(factor, 0) * weight for factor, weight in factor_weights.items())

# Define a threshold to decide between "YES" and "NO"
threshold = 3

# Predict the outcome
if risk_score >= threshold:
    prediction = "YES"
else:
    prediction = "NO"

print(f"Risk Score: {risk_score}")
print(f"Prediction: {prediction}")
```

### Explanation

1. **Factor Weights:** We assign weights to each factor based on their perceived impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
2. **Individual Profile:** We create a dictionary representing the individual's characteristics.
3. **Risk Score Calculation:** Multiply the individual's factor values by their respective weights and sum them up to get the risk score.
4. **Prediction:** If the risk score meets or exceeds a predefined threshold, predict "YES" for rearrest; otherwise, predict "NO."

In this case, the individual has a risk score of 2, which is below the threshold of 3, leading to a prediction of "NO" for rearrest within three years.

## Final Solution
To predict whether a 20-year-old Hispanic male will be rearrested within three years, we need to analyze various factors based on provided examples. These factors include demographic information, criminal history, personal life, education and employment, substance use, mental health, family background, and religious beliefs.

### Approach

1. **Identify Key Factors:** Examine which factors are most influential in determining rearrest outcomes.
2. **Pattern Recognition:** Look for trends in the examples provided to understand how different combinations of factors lead to "YES" or "NO" outcomes.
3. **Risk Assessment:** Assign weights to each factor to quantify their impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
4. **Comparison:** Compare the given individual's profile to the examples and calculate a risk score.

### Solution Code

Since this is a predictive analysis based on qualitative data, there isn't a specific code to run. However, we can structure our analysis in a step-by-step manner.

```python
# Define the factors and their potential impact scores
factor_weights = {
    'arrests': 2,          # Each arrest adds 2 points
    'conviction': 3,       # Conviction adds 3 points
    'drug_use': 2,         # Drug use adds 2 points
    'depression': 1,       # Depression adds 1 point
    'living_alone': 1,     # Living alone adds 1 point
    'no_job': 2,           # No job adds 2 points
    'lower_education': 1,  # Lower education adds 1 point
    'no_enrollment': 1,    # No recent enrollment adds 1 point
    'god_influence': -1    # Belief in God's influence subtracts 1 point
}

# Individual's profile
individual_profile = {
    'arrests': 1,
    'conviction': 0,
    'drug_use': 0,
    'depression': 0,
    'living_alone': 0,
    'no_job': 0,
    'lower_education': 0,
    'no_enrollment': 0,
    'god_influence': 0
}

# Calculate the risk score
risk_score = sum(individual_profile.get(factor, 0) * weight for factor, weight in factor_weights.items())

# Define a threshold to decide between "YES" and "NO"
threshold = 3

# Predict the outcome
if risk_score >= threshold:
    prediction = "YES"
else:
    prediction = "NO"

print(f"Risk Score: {risk_score}")
print(f"Prediction: {prediction}")
```

### Explanation

1. **Factor Weights:** We assign weights to each factor based on their perceived impact on the likelihood of rearrest.
2. **Individual Profile:** We create a dictionary representing the individual's characteristics.
3. **Risk Score Calculation:** Multiply the individual's factor values by their respective weights and sum them up to get the risk score.
4. **Prediction:** If the risk score meets or exceeds a predefined threshold, predict "YES" for rearrest; otherwise, predict "NO."

In this case, the individual has a risk score of 2, which is below the threshold of 3, leading to a prediction of "NO" for rearrest within three years.
